< Review>
Good food, decent ambiance and great customer service. The place is unique in the sense of the ambiance. It has both indoor and outdoor seating but when I went, it was cold. The server was super nice and friendly. The food was good but the servings were not huge, I guess I got used to big servings (which is not necessarily great). The aji was good but a bit different from what I had at other restaurants. My lomo saltado was tender and juicy. Overall, good place but a bit hidden. The restaurant does have parking in the back though. The only thing I didn't like was the no refills on drinks. All of the drinks come in cans or bottles. Besides that, great customer service.<//Review>

< text>
I've had great experiences with this location!  They do not have a big lot on-site (they pull cars from remote locations), so it's best to communicate with them a few hours or a day in advance to make sure they can have the vehicle you need on-hand when you arrive (also confirm the deposit and full amount they will need to authorize to make sure your credit card company will approve the charge- that's common sense renting from anywhere these days, especially with overly-paranoid fraud protection depts at CC companies, and their deposit is lower than most!)  Everyone in their staff has been helpful and honest, and the Manager, Michael, has gone above and beyond what was expected for me and friends I've convinced to rent from there in the past, and so has Anthony! Their office is adjoined to a body shop, and they have a small waiting area, so if you can come during less-busy hours, there's usually no wait. If you come right when they open or when people traditionally drop their cars off next door (before/after work or lunchtime), you get the luck of the draw in terms of your wait time.  But the staff and rates are worth customers having to plan ahead a bit and communicate with them (don't expect websites and apps to provide all the info and functions that people do. üòâ)<//text>

<name>Nikki Kuppens<//name><date>1545899799584<//date>< Rate>
1</Rate>
< text>
This is a review for this location in particular, but also partly for Hertz as a whole. We reserved (and paid for) a convertible 5 months in advance, but it turns out this location's availability just depends on whatever cars get returned to them. So it doesn't matter if you reserve months or days in advance, if no car of the type you reserved is there on the day of pickup, you're just screwed. The Hertz head office does not make sure reservations are filled, so at this location they just try to send you off in any of the cars that are available. They do work together with some other locations around LA, but this does not include the airport. The manager and staff have accepted the fact that they can't rely on Hertz's overall fleet and will do nothing for you to make things right. When we came to pick up our car, pretty much nobody left in the car they reserved, including families that were offered 2 separate midsize cars instead of the van or SUV they paid for (and having only 1 driver available).

We begrudgingly accepted a regular car so we could continue our carefully planned road trip, being told that we would be able to swap it out for a convertible at any Hertz location. We spent way too much time on the phone with customer service, online with social media support and visiting several locations, including LAX. The issue is that customer service is completely out of touch with how individual offices operate. It turned out that both LAX and McCarran airport in Vegas had been sitting on many convertibles, but didn't want to hand out any because they were going for a premium due to ComicCon and several sports events. So while customer service will tell you that you can swap out the car anywhere and slightly help with checking availability, the individual locations are just looking out for their own interest and won't help filling a reservation that another location failed to deliver on.

In the end, we finally got out convertible after a lot of arguing at McCarran. We immediately changed our drop off location to LAX instead of this Pico office, because we didn't want to deal with the unhelpful and indifferent staff at that location. Apart from a free tank of gas (which we ended up not even getting), we were never offered any form of compensation, either from this location or after filing a complaint with Hertz. In the future we'll try to avoid renting from Hertz, but if you for some reason have to stick to them, don't rent from a location other than airports. It will be more expensive, but it's not worth the hassle if things go wrong.< /text>

< Review>
Our stay at The Ranch far exceeded our expectations.  We arrived at 3pm on a Friday, check in wasn't until 4pm, but our room was already ready.  There isn't self parking available to check in, but the wonderful valet staff (talking about you Andrew) will pull your car forward and have it waiting for you when you find out where your room is.  The check in process is quick and pleasant, the room RFID room keys are not plastic, but bamboo, a nice touch.  We reserved a creek view suite, the view from the room was amazing, between the fish in the bubbling creek, and the red tailed hawks overhead, we had our morning coffee and tea outside every day.  I highly recommend the garden tour on Saturday as well, reservations are required.  Louis, the Gardener, was extremely informative about everything he produces, and most of the produce is used in the meals made on property.  The food at Harvest is also epic.  I'm a pretty slim guy, but between the Wagyu steak, many seafood dishes, half chicken, I powered through all of my meals even though I was full.  It's THAT good.  Wait staff is amazing, always accommodating to your every need.  I also highly recommend room service for breakfast.  You actually order it on a tablet in your room, no phone call necessary.  My wife's egg whites were more airy and fluffier than she's ever had, and we've stayed at some amazing places.  Just an FYI, there is absolutely zero cell phone service, you have to connect to the free WiFi to make calls.  My wife's phone worked great for calls on WiFi, mine did not at first, but Anthony at the front desk is a genius.  I'm an IT guy and couldn't get my phone to work for calls over WiFi, Anthony gave me some advice and it worked perfectly after that.  Honestly though, I'd recommend enjoying the dead zone and decompressing without a phone for a few days.  My wife came down with a cold about two hours before we arrived.  The Amazing front desk manager Jenn pulled out a whole box of cold remedies to help her.  Jenn was incredibly accommodating, thoughtful, and made us feel so welcoming every time we saw her with her work ethic, bright and genuine smile, she went above and beyond to make out stay memorable.  We usually do staycations at Pechanga, Santa Barbara, San Diego at the Bay Club, no more.  We're going to The Ranch for every Staycation from now on out. <review>We stayed for 2 nights in a two bedroom suite. The location was secluded and peaceful, and the staff was friendly, welcoming, and helpful. We enjoyed a casual outdoor dinner with live music at Ben's Pantry and an outstanding more formal dinner at Harvest restaurant. We had a great time with our son at the beach across the street (Aliso Beach). <review>Wow, what a hidden gem. This place is nested in Laguna beach between the canyons on a golf course. It looks like a lodge you would find in the mountains and is extremely well kept.

< Review>
A beautiful place that is undergoing renovation.

Our room was beautiful, and the staff was nice. The food was also spectacular.

Where they fell short was Guest Service. When you call there, you have to go through voicemail to get to your first live person, who may well transfer you to voicemail for the person/department you're looking for. There also wasn't a hotel directory or a restaurant menu in the room, and nothing for nearby activities.

I spent most of my life working in the Guest Service industry, though not in the Guest Service department. One phrase I learned to hate is "Not a problem" as a response to "Thank you." I only heard it once, and it rubbed the wrong way.  Overall, it was a great stay though, and we'd like to stay there again.<//Review>

<resp>None< /resp>< Review>
My mother and I came to The Ranch for a girls weekend and could not have been more disappointed. Upon check-in, we were greeted and told that we had to enable Wi-Fi calling at which time the receptionist looked to my mom, then to me, and said I would probably know how to do it, insinuating my mother was tech-incapable. Since our room was not yet ready, the receptionist stated the number they had on file to call when it was ready. I gave her a different number, informing her the number on file was our house phone. Still, my father informed us that they called our house to tell us our room was ready. We went to the Harvest restaurant following check-in and had to send our well-done request back when it was served cut in half and very pink. We visited the restaurant 2 more times and each time they forgot some aspect of our order and neglected to give us utensils. We got a treatment at their Sycamore Spa and the experience was uncomfortable. The masseuse repeatedly put my extremities on his stomach and the massage was incredibly poor. One evening we interacted with an employee who asked about our stay. When we mentioned our list of problems about the restaurant, he candidly responded that he actually had heard this many times before. Finally, during turndown service they took our towels and did not leave replacements. When we called for towels, it took over an hour for them to deliver the items. I strongly advise you look elsewhere for a relaxing stay.< /Review>

Eden Jeffries<//user_name>
<Response>None< /Response><Date>1484003011555</Date><review>A beautiful and peaceful retreat tucked inside of the coastal hillside of Laguna. It has the feel of an upscale cottage resort in the mountains but less than a mile from the beach. The rooms are spacious and wonderfully designed. There is a restaurant  and a cafe, both with beautiful views of the mountainside and gold course. The restaurant (Harvest) has a menu of upscale Contemporary American cuisine featuring fresh produce from the on-site garden. The cafe (Ben's Pantry) has espresso drinks, pastries, beer, wine, cocktails and gourmet food dishes. There is a daily happy hour as well at Ben's Pantry with $10 food items like steak skewers, chile lime chicken quesadilla, charcuterie plate, burger and fries, and more.
The pool is heated year-round. The fitness room can be accessed 24 hours and has all the basic machines and resistance equipment. I was very well taken care of here and certainly prefer this place to stay over many of the beach hotels for the amenities, the quality of the rooms and the quaintness.<//review>< Rating>

<review>We took the family for a Saturday night stay last weekend, looking forward to checking out another luxury hotel in SoCal.
As we were driving up the little road to the hotel, I jokingly told my wife "maybe the driveway is so unappealing as to try to improve your impression of the hotel". When we saw the hotel, I think I was right. Yes, the canyon is picturesque, but the hotel grounds and the renovated buildings (color and style) were not astheticly pleasing at all. Not sure what the designer was going for. From there it was hit and miss. The rooms are newly renovated and nicely furnished, but the old windows and sliding doors represent economy and not luxury.
In addition, the pool was not heated enough (76 degrees I was told), the only food the pool bar had available was a big container of Chex mix, and the food at the club house was really quite average. The staff were friendly but there clearly were not enough staff at the restaurant or assisting with the pool bar.
If your expectations are low and you don't buy in to previous reviews , you may enjoy the hotel.
Unfortunately a generally disappointing experience for us.< /review>< pictures>
None<//pictures>
